The error is clear: CocoaPods isn't installed, and your Flutter plugins (Firebase, Google Maps, etc.) need it to work on iOS/macOS. Let me check your environment and fix this.

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
Flutter uses CocoaPods as a dependency manager for native iOS/macOS code. When plugins include platform-specific (Objective-C/Swift) code, CocoaPods resolves and links those native dependencies — similar to how `pub` manages Dart packages, CocoaPods manages the native side.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

CocoaPods is missing. Let me install it via Homebrew (more reliable than the system Ruby gem on modern macOS).

---

CocoaPods is installed. Now let me run `pod install` for the macOS target and verify everything works.

---

Still downloading dependencies. Let me wait for it to finish.

---

Pod install completed successfully. Let me check the full output to confirm.

---

Pod install succeeded (23 pods installed), but there are configuration warnings. The Xcode project has custom configs that need to include the CocoaPods configs. Let me fix that.

---

I need to include the CocoaPods-generated xcconfig files in the Debug and Release configs. Let me also check if there's a Profile config.

---

Now let me check if there's a Profile xcconfig that also needs updating. Flutter uses Profile for profile builds.

---

No separate Profile Flutter xcconfig — the profile build likely uses the Release config. The CocoaPods warning about profile config should resolve since the project only has Debug and Release build configs mapped.

Now let's try running the app.

---

The build failed with `clang: error: unsupported option '-G'`. This is a known issue with BoringSSL/gRPC on newer Xcode versions. Let me check the Podfile and fix the deployment target issue, which is the root cause.

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

Flutter uses CocoaPods as a dependency manager for native iOS/macOS code. When plugins include platform-specific (Objective-C/Swift) code, CocoaPods resolves and links those native dependencies — similar to how `pub` manages Dart packages, CocoaPods manages the native side.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

CocoaPods is missing. Let me install it via Homebrew (more reliable than the system Ruby gem on modern macOS).

---

---

No separate Profile Flutter xcconfig — the profile build likely uses the Release config. The CocoaPods warning about profile config should resolve since the project only has Debug and Release build configs mapped.

Now let's try running the app.

---

The build failed with `clang: error: unsupported option '-G'`. This is a known issue with BoringSSL/gRPC on newer Xcode versions. Let me check the Podfile and fix the deployment target issue, which is the root cause.

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

The build failed with `clang: error: unsupported option '-G'`. This is a known issue with BoringSSL/gRPC on newer Xcode versions. Let me check the Podfile and fix the deployment target issue, which is the root cause.

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`

- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

You can now run the app with `flutter run -d macos`.

>>> llm 2026-05-22 15:41:11
The error is clear: CocoaPods isn't installed, and your Flutter plugins (Firebase, Google Maps, etc.) need it to work on iOS/macOS. Let me check your environment and fix this.

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
Flutter uses CocoaPods as a dependency manager for native iOS/macOS code. When plugins include platform-specific (Objective-C/Swift) code, CocoaPods resolves and links those native dependencies — similar to how `pub` manages Dart packages, CocoaPods manages the native side.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

CocoaPods is missing. Let me install it via Homebrew (more reliable than the system Ruby gem on modern macOS).

---

No separate Profile Flutter xcconfig — the profile build likely uses the Release config. The CocoaPods warning about profile config should resolve since the project only has Debug and Release build configs mapped.

Now let's try running the app.

---

The build failed with `clang: error: unsupported option '-G'`. This is a known issue with BoringSSL/gRPC on newer Xcode versions. Let me check the Podfile and fix the deployment target issue, which is the root cause.

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

There's only one error, repeated across files. The gRPC-Core code uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang flags as an error. I need to add `-Wno-missing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` to the gRPC-Core build settings.

---

No errors! Let me check the build result.

---

The build succeeded! The app compiled to `build/macos/Build/Products/Release/vysion_omnigod.app` (101.4MB).

Here's a summary of what was fixed:

1. **Installed CocoaPods** via Homebrew (`brew install cocoapods`)
2. **Added CocoaPods xcconfig includes** to `macos/Runner/Configs/Debug.xcconfig` and `Release.xcconfig` so the build system can find pod dependencies
3. **Fixed the `-G` flag error** in the Podfile's `post_install` — BoringSSL-GRPC's podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag, but Xcode 26's stricter clang parses `-G` as an unsupported standalone option
4. **Suppressed the `-Wmissing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` error** — gRPC-Core uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang (Xcode 26+) promotes to an error

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

You can now run the app with `flutter run -d macos`.

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

2. **Added CocoaPods xcconfig includes** to `macos/Runner/Configs/Debug.xcconfig` and `Release.xcconfig` so the build system can find pod dependencies
3. **Fixed the `-G` flag error** in the Podfile's `post_install` — BoringSSL-GRPC's podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag, but Xcode 26's stricter clang parses `-G` as an unsupported standalone option
4. **Suppressed the `-Wmissing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` error** — gRPC-Core uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang (Xcode 26+) promotes to an error

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.

Adding the required `NSLocationUsageDescription` to the macOS Info.plist.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- macOS uses `NSLocationUsageDescription` (singular) while iOS uses `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription` or `NSLocationAlwaysUsageDescription`. The `geolocator` plugin checks for the platform-appropriate key at runtime and throws if it's missing.
- The string value is what macOS shows the user in the permission dialog — it should explain *why* the app needs location access.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

The flag has been stripped. Let's build now.

The build succeeded! The app compiled to `build/macos/Build/Products/Release/vysion_omnigod.app` (101.4MB).

Here's a summary of what was fixed:

1. **Installed CocoaPods** via Homebrew (`brew install cocoapods`)
2. **Added CocoaPods xcconfig includes** to `macos/Runner/Configs/Debug.xcconfig` and `Release.xcconfig` so the build system can find pod dependencies
3. **Fixed the `-G` flag error** in the Podfile's `post_install` — BoringSSL-GRPC's podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag, but Xcode 26's stricter clang parses `-G` as an unsupported standalone option
4. **Suppressed the `-Wmissing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` error** — gRPC-Core uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang (Xcode 26+) promotes to an error

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

Adding the required `NSLocationUsageDescription` to the macOS Info.plist.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- macOS uses `NSLocationUsageDescription` (singular) while iOS uses `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription` or `NSLocationAlwaysUsageDescription`. The `geolocator` plugin checks for the platform-appropriate key at runtime and throws if it's missing.
- The string value is what macOS shows the user in the permission dialog — it should explain *why* the app needs location access.

---

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

---

The `_requestingPermissions` flag was set to `true` from a previous run but never reset — so now every tap hits the early `return`. Since you hot-reloaded (not hot-restarted), the state persisted. But the real fix is to ensure the flag gets reset properly.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The original code set the guard flag but never cleared it. If the permission request completed (or threw), the flag stayed `true` forever — making the button permanently dead. Wrapping in `try/finally` ensures the flag resets regardless of success or failure.
- This is a common pattern with async guard flags: always reset in `finally`, not after the happy path.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed — the flag now resets in a `finally` block. Do a hot-restart (capital `R` in the terminal) to clear the old state and try the button again.

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

The build succeeded! The app compiled to `build/macos/Build/Products/Release/vysion_omnigod.app` (101.4MB).

Here's a summary of what was fixed:

1. **Installed CocoaPods** via Homebrew (`brew install cocoapods`)
2. **Added CocoaPods xcconfig includes** to `macos/Runner/Configs/Debug.xcconfig` and `Release.xcconfig` so the build system can find pod dependencies
3. **Fixed the `-G` flag error** in the Podfile's `post_install` — BoringSSL-GRPC's podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag, but Xcode 26's stricter clang parses `-G` as an unsupported standalone option
4. **Suppressed the `-Wmissing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` error** — gRPC-Core uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang (Xcode 26+) promotes to an error

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

You can now run the app with `flutter run -d macos`.

---

Adding the required `NSLocationUsageDescription` to the macOS Info.plist.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- macOS uses `NSLocationUsageDescription` (singular) while iOS uses `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription` or `NSLocationAlwaysUsageDescription`. The `geolocator` plugin checks for the platform-appropriate key at runtime and throws if it's missing.
- The string value is what macOS shows the user in the permission dialog — it should explain *why* the app needs location access.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Added `NSLocationUsageDescription` to `macos/Runner/Info.plist`. Rebuild and the location permission error should be resolved.

---

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

---

The `_requestingPermissions` flag was set to `true` from a previous run but never reset — so now every tap hits the early `return`. Since you hot-reloaded (not hot-restarted), the state persisted. But the real fix is to ensure the flag gets reset properly.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The original code set the guard flag but never cleared it. If the permission request completed (or threw), the flag stayed `true` forever — making the button permanently dead. Wrapping in `try/finally` ensures the flag resets regardless of success or failure.
- This is a common pattern with async guard flags: always reset in `finally`, not after the happy path.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed — the flag now resets in a `finally` block. Do a hot-restart (capital `R` in the terminal) to clear the old state and try the button again.

---

The guard flag isn't working because the `Semantics` `onTap` and the `ElevatedButton` `onPressed` are both firing simultaneously on each tap. Two calls enter before the first `await` sets the flag. Let me fix both issues — remove the duplicate trigger and make the guard synchronous-safe.

The build failed with `clang: error: unsupported option '-G'`. This is a known issue with BoringSSL/gRPC on newer Xcode versions. Let me check the Podfile and fix the deployment target issue, which is the root cause.

---

The `-G` flag error is a known issue with BoringSSL-GRPC on newer Xcode/macOS versions (Xcode 26+). I need to add a post-install hook that removes the unsupported `-G` flag and also bumps deployment targets for pods that are too low.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now let me re-run pod install and build.

---

The warnings about base configurations are expected since we already included them via the Debug.xcconfig and Release.xcconfig includes. Let me try building again.

---

The `-G` flag is still present — it's coming from the BoringSSL-GRPC pod's `OTHER_CFLAGS` in the xcconfig, and the regex-based approach in the post_install wasn't sufficient. Let me take a more thorough approach by also stripping it from build settings directly.

---

The `-G` flag isn't in the xcconfig files — it must be in the podspec or the Xcode project directly. Let me search more broadly.

---

Found it! The `-G` is part of `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` in the COMPILER_FLAGS. That's not the actual `-G` flag — it's a substring match issue. Let me look more carefully at the actual error.

---

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

---

Wait — I ran `pod install` from the wrong directory (my working directory may not be `macos/`). Let me be explicit.

---

Good, pod install succeeded. Now let's verify the fix was applied and build again.

---

The flag has been stripped. Let's build now.

---

Still failing. Let me see the actual errors more clearly.

---

A different error now — the `-G` flag is fixed. This is a C++ template syntax issue in gRPC-Core with the newer clang in Xcode 26. Let me suppress this warning being treated as an error.

---

There's only one error, repeated across files. The gRPC-Core code uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang flags as an error. I need to add `-Wno-missing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` to the gRPC-Core build settings.

---

No errors! Let me check the build result.

---

The build succeeded! The app compiled to `build/macos/Build/Products/Release/vysion_omnigod.app` (101.4MB).

Here's a summary of what was fixed:

1. **Installed CocoaPods** via Homebrew (`brew install cocoapods`)
2. **Added CocoaPods xcconfig includes** to `macos/Runner/Configs/Debug.xcconfig` and `Release.xcconfig` so the build system can find pod dependencies
3. **Fixed the `-G` flag error** in the Podfile's `post_install` — BoringSSL-GRPC's podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag, but Xcode 26's stricter clang parses `-G` as an unsupported standalone option
4. **Suppressed the `-Wmissing-template-arg-list-after-template-kw` error** — gRPC-Core uses a deprecated C++ template syntax that newer clang (Xcode 26+) promotes to an error

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.
- The `DART_DEFINES` "Invalid key/value pair" warnings during `pod install` are cosmetic and don't affect the build.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

You can now run the app with `flutter run -d macos`.

---

Adding the required `NSLocationUsageDescription` to the macOS Info.plist.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- macOS uses `NSLocationUsageDescription` (singular) while iOS uses `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription` or `NSLocationAlwaysUsageDescription`. The `geolocator` plugin checks for the platform-appropriate key at runtime and throws if it's missing.
- The string value is what macOS shows the user in the permission dialog — it should explain *why* the app needs location access.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Added `NSLocationUsageDescription` to `macos/Runner/Info.plist`. Rebuild and the location permission error should be resolved.

---

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

---

The `_requestingPermissions` flag was set to `true` from a previous run but never reset — so now every tap hits the early `return`. Since you hot-reloaded (not hot-restarted), the state persisted. But the real fix is to ensure the flag gets reset properly.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The original code set the guard flag but never cleared it. If the permission request completed (or threw), the flag stayed `true` forever — making the button permanently dead. Wrapping in `try/finally` ensures the flag resets regardless of success or failure.
- This is a common pattern with async guard flags: always reset in `finally`, not after the happy path.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed — the flag now resets in a `finally` block. Do a hot-restart (capital `R` in the terminal) to clear the old state and try the button again.

---

The guard flag isn't working because the `Semantics` `onTap` and the `ElevatedButton` `onPressed` are both firing simultaneously on each tap. Two calls enter before the first `await` sets the flag. Let me fix both issues — remove the duplicate trigger and make the guard synchronous-safe.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `Semantics(onTap: ...)` and `ElevatedButton(onPressed: ...)` were both wired to `_requestPermissions`. A single user tap triggered *both* callbacks — the Semantics gesture handler and the button's own `onPressed` — causing two concurrent `requestPermission()` calls. 
- `ElevatedButton` already generates its own semantics actions, so the outer `Semantics` widget only needs to provide the custom `label` — not a duplicate `onTap`.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Removed the duplicate `onTap` from the `Semantics` wrapper. The `ElevatedButton.onPressed` is the single entry point now. Hot-restart and try again.

---

Yes — but the root issue is likely that macOS entitlements for location aren't configured, so the system never shows a dialog and the plugin gets stuck. Let me check.

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `-G` flag is a linker option for grouping that gRPC/BoringSSL uses on Linux but is unsupported by Apple's clang. Newer Xcode versions (26+) are stricter about unknown flags.
- The `post_install` hook in the Podfile runs after CocoaPods finishes installing — it's the standard place to patch build settings that upstream pods don't set correctly for your environment.
- We also bump `MACOSX_DEPLOYMENT_TARGET` to 10.15 for all pods because macOS 10.11/10.12 targets are rejected by the current Xcode toolchain.

The `-G` isn't in the xcconfig. Let me check if it's coming from the BoringSSL podspec's compiler flags embedded in the pbxproj per-file settings.

---

Now I see it! The COMPILER_FLAGS contain `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` which is an Xcode build setting, not a compiler flag. Newer Xcode is parsing `-G` as a standalone flag and then `CC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a file. This is a bug in the BoringSSL-GRPC podspec.

The fix is to modify the post_install to strip `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` from per-file compiler flags in the Xcode project, or better yet, use the `post_install` to modify the build settings on the target itself.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The BoringSSL-GRPC podspec uses `-GCC_WARN_INHIBIT_ALL_WARNINGS` as a per-file compiler flag. This is actually an Xcode build setting (not a clang flag). Older Xcode versions tolerated it, but Xcode 26+ treats `-G` as a standalone unsupported option.
- The `source_build_phase.files` API lets you modify per-file compiler flags in the CocoaPods-generated Xcode project, which is where these flags live (not in xcconfig files).
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- These are all compatibility issues between older Firebase/gRPC pod versions and the latest Xcode 26 toolchain. Upgrading to newer Firebase SDK versions (11.x+) would fix most of these at the source.
- The remaining warnings about Swift Package Manager adoption are informational — those plugins will need to migrate from CocoaPods to SPM in a future Flutter version, but they work fine for now.

Adding the required `NSLocationUsageDescription` to the macOS Info.plist.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- macOS uses `NSLocationUsageDescription` (singular) while iOS uses `NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription` or `NSLocationAlwaysUsageDescription`. The `geolocator` plugin checks for the platform-appropriate key at runtime and throws if it's missing.
- The string value is what macOS shows the user in the permission dialog — it should explain *why* the app needs location access.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Added `NSLocationUsageDescription` to `macos/Runner/Info.plist`. Rebuild and the location permission error should be resolved.

---

The `_requestPermissions` method is being called multiple times concurrently. Let me fix it.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `geolocator` plugin uses a single native channel for permission requests. Calling `requestPermission()` while one is already in flight throws. A simple boolean guard prevents duplicate calls — no need for a `Completer` or mutex here since Flutter's UI thread is single-threaded and the guard is checked synchronously before the first `await`.
- The button's `onPressed` fires on each tap, and the `Semantics` widget's `onTap` can also trigger it independently — two entry points to the same async method.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed. The `_requestPermissions` method now guards against concurrent calls with a boolean flag. Hot-restart to pick up the change.

---

The `_requestingPermissions` flag was set to `true` from a previous run but never reset — so now every tap hits the early `return`. Since you hot-reloaded (not hot-restarted), the state persisted. But the real fix is to ensure the flag gets reset properly.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The original code set the guard flag but never cleared it. If the permission request completed (or threw), the flag stayed `true` forever — making the button permanently dead. Wrapping in `try/finally` ensures the flag resets regardless of success or failure.
- This is a common pattern with async guard flags: always reset in `finally`, not after the happy path.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Fixed — the flag now resets in a `finally` block. Do a hot-restart (capital `R` in the terminal) to clear the old state and try the button again.

---

The guard flag isn't working because the `Semantics` `onTap` and the `ElevatedButton` `onPressed` are both firing simultaneously on each tap. Two calls enter before the first `await` sets the flag. Let me fix both issues — remove the duplicate trigger and make the guard synchronous-safe.

---

`★ Insight ─────────────────────────────────────`
- The `Semantics(onTap: ...)` and `ElevatedButton(onPressed: ...)` were both wired to `_requestPermissions`. A single user tap triggered *both* callbacks — the Semantics gesture handler and the button's own `onPressed` — causing two concurrent `requestPermission()` calls. 
- `ElevatedButton` already generates its own semantics actions, so the outer `Semantics` widget only needs to provide the custom `label` — not a duplicate `onTap`.
`─────────────────────────────────────────────────`

Removed the duplicate `onTap` from the `Semantics` wrapper. The `ElevatedButton.onPressed` is the single entry point now. Hot-restart and try again.

---

Yes — but the root issue is likely that macOS entitlements for location aren't configured, so the system never shows a dialog and the plugin gets stuck. Let me check.
